(4) Li Shizeng was appointed to present a report at the Central Commemoration Week next Monday. (13th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Organizational Law of the National Congress 50

(Nanjing) The Central Standing Committee held its 66th meeting on the morning of the 13th and approved the Organizational Law of the Provisional National Congress. The original text is as follows: Organizational Law of the Provisional National Congress of the Kuomintang of China, Article 1: The Provisional National Congress is organized by party member representatives legally produced by party headquarters in various regions. The qualifications of the aforementioned representatives shall be reviewed by the Representative Qualification Review Committee organized by the Central Executive Committee. Article 2: When the Provisional National Congress is convened, members of the Central Executive Committee and members of the Central Supervisory Committee may attend. Alternate members of the Central Executive Committee and alternate members of the Central Supervisory Committee may be present. Article 3: The Provisional National Congress shall establish a presidium, which shall be proposed by the Central Executive Committee and organized with the approval of the Congress. Article 4: The Provisional National Congress shall establish a secretariat to handle all affairs under the order of the Congress Presidium. Its organization shall be determined separately. Article 5: The term of the Provisional National Congress shall be seven days, but it may be extended if necessary. Article 6: The Provisional National Congress must have more than half of the representatives present to convene. Decisions of the Congress shall be made with the consent of more than half of the representatives present. The question of approval or rejection shall be determined by the chair. Article 7: The meetings of the Provisional National Congress may be held in secret when necessary, as decided by the Presidium or requested by more than 40 representatives. Article 8: The rules of procedure of the Provisional National Congress shall be determined separately. Article 9: The Provisional National Congress may establish various committees. Article 10: The expenses of the Provisional National Congress shall be determined by the Central Executive Committee. Article 11: This organizational law shall be implemented upon the decision of the Central Executive Committee. (13th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Election Law of the National Congress 51

(Nanjing) The Central Standing Committee held its 66th meeting on the morning of the 13th and approved the articles of the Election Law for Representatives of the Provisional National Congress as follows: Article 1: The election of representatives to the Provisional National Congress shall be conducted in accordance with this law. Article 2: The total number of representatives to the Provisional National Congress is set at 426, and the distribution is as shown in the attached table. Article 3: The election of representatives to the Provisional National Congress shall use a multiple-round election system. County and city party headquarters in provinces and district branches in special municipalities shall be the primary election organs. Provincial and special municipal party headquarters shall be the secondary election organs. Overseas, branch offices and directly affiliated branches shall be the primary election organs, and the general branch shall be the secondary election organ. For directly affiliated branches, the branch offices shall be the primary election organs, and the directly affiliated branch shall be the secondary election organ. Article 4: Electors and those eligible to be elected shall be limited to party members holding party membership cards. Those elected in the secondary election are not limited to those elected in the primary election. Article 5: The election of representatives to local party headquarters or special party headquarters shall be directly elected by the primary election representatives according to the number stipulated by the central government. However, in special municipalities, party members may directly vote to elect. Article 6: Each county, city, and special party headquarters directly under the province with fewer than 100 party members shall elect one primary election representative. Those with 100 or more but fewer than 300 shall elect two. Those with 300 or more shall elect three, but no more than three. District party headquarters directly under the province may elect one primary election representative. Party members belonging to the district branch directly under the province shall be designated by the provincial party headquarters to join the neighboring county party headquarters for a combined election. Article 7: The standards for the number of primary election representatives for overseas general branch offices are as follows: A. For party members below 1,000, each branch office or directly affiliated branch office with fewer than 50 party members shall elect two primary election representatives; those with fewer than 100 shall elect three; and one shall be added for every additional 50, but no more than five. B. For party members below 5,000, each branch office or directly affiliated branch office with fewer than 100 party members shall elect one primary election representative; those with 100 or more shall elect two; and one shall be added for every additional 100, but no more than six. C. For party members above 5,000, each branch office or directly affiliated branch office with fewer than 200 party members shall elect one primary election representative; those with fewer than 400 shall elect two; and one shall be added for every additional 200, but no more than seven. Overseas direct branch offices or direct district branch offices with fewer than 30 members shall elect one primary election representative; those with 30 or more shall elect two; and one shall be added for every additional 30, but no more than four. Article 8: The election of representatives of special party headquarters in the military shall be carried out by the central government submitting a number of candidates, which shall be printed by each special party headquarters and issued to the company party headquarters. The election shall be conducted using a signed ballot from among the candidates submitted by the central government. Article 9: The election of representatives of special party headquarters for sailors and railways shall be directly voted on by party members belonging to each party headquarters, with the district branch serving as the election district. Article 10: Primary and secondary elections shall be conducted using signed ballots. Overseas party headquarters may use postal methods with the approval of the central government. Article 11: For remote provinces and districts or places with special circumstances, the production of representatives shall be decided by the Central Executive Committee. Article 12: When handling elections, the primary election organs shall first announce the party member roster, the number of primary election representatives, the election date, and the voting method to the party members, and may divide the voting by region according to the distribution of party members. After voting, the ballots shall be opened and the number of votes obtained by the elected candidates and the election ballots shall be sent to the election handling organ for combined counting. Article 13: After producing the primary election representatives, each primary election organ shall immediately report the names and mailing addresses of the representatives directly to the secondary election organ. Article 14: After completing the secondary election, each secondary election organ shall immediately report the list of elected candidates and the election situation to the central government and issue certificates to the elected candidates. Article 15: If the number of votes is the same after the ballot opening, the election handling organ shall determine the winner by lottery. Article 16: Anyone with one of the following circumstances shall not be elected as a representative: (1) Those who have violated the party's words or deeds. (2) Those who have been expelled from the party or suspended from party rights. Article 17: If it is discovered after the representative is produced that there is election fraud or that there are circumstances as described in the preceding article, in addition to the central government revoking their representative status and giving appropriate punishment, the next most-voted candidate shall replace them. Article 18: The quota and election deadline for representatives from various regions shall be determined separately. Article 19: The Central Executive Committee shall have the highest interpretation right for this election law. Article 20: This election law shall be implemented upon the decision of the Central Executive Committee. The distribution of quotas for representatives to the Provisional National Congress is as follows: (1) 249 shall be elected by provincial and municipal party headquarters; (2) 88 shall be elected by overseas party headquarters; (3) 60 shall be elected by special party headquarters in the military; (4) 13 shall be elected by special party headquarters for sailors and railways; (5) 16 shall be produced by remote provinces and districts. (13th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Organizational Regulations for the Congress Secretariat 52

(Nanjing) The Central Standing Committee held its 66th meeting on the morning of the 13th and approved the Organizational Regulations for the Secretariat of the Provisional National Congress. The original text is as follows: Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with Article 4 of the Organizational Law of the Provisional National Congress. Article 2: The Secretariat shall have one Secretary-General and four to six secretaries, who shall handle the affairs of the Secretariat under the order of the Presidium. The candidates shall first be appointed by the Central Executive Committee and submitted to the Congress for ratification. Article 3: The Secretariat shall have the following sections: Document Section, Procedural Section, Reception Section, Accounting Section, and General Affairs Section. Each section may have several divisions according to the situation of affairs. Article 4: The duties of the Document Section are as follows: (1) Drafting, receiving, dispatching, copying, and storing documents. (2) Supervising the use of seals. (3) Preparing and issuing meeting notices. (4) Editing the Congress Gazette and other promotional materials. (5) Other documentation matters related to the Congress and the Secretariat. Article 5: The duties of the Procedural Section are as follows: (1) Compiling the agenda. (2) Recording the meetings of the Congress and various committees. (3) Compiling the minutes of the Congress and various committees. (4) Assisting in the review and sorting of proposals and resolutions. (5) Printing of meeting documents. (6) Other meeting matters related to the Congress and various committees. Article 6: The duties of the Reception Section are as follows: (1) Representative registration and registration matters. (2) Preparing representative accommodation and other necessary supplies. (3) Guiding representatives for tours and visits. (4) Providing care and assistance in the meeting venue. (5) Producing, issuing, and inspecting attendance permits. (6) Receiving guests and journalists. (7) Other reception matters related to the Congress and the Secretariat. Article 7: The duties of the Accounting Section are as follows: (1) Receipt, payment, and safekeeping of funds. (2) Auditing various accounts. (3) Preparing expense reports. (4) Other financial matters related to the Congress and the Secretariat. Article 8: The duties of the General Affairs Section are as follows: (1) Preparing and arranging meeting venues. (2) Purchasing and storing all application items. (3) Producing and issuing various badges. (4) Managing security and labor affairs. (5) Other matters not belonging to other sections. Article 9: Each section shall have one section chief, who shall be appointed by the Central Executive Committee upon the proposal of the Secretary-General, to manage the affairs of the section. Article 10: Under each section chief, there shall be several directors, officers, assistants, and clerks, all of whom shall be appointed by the Secretary-General from qualified personnel. Article 11: All staff members of the Secretariat, from the section chiefs downwards, shall be transferred from the working staff of various offices of the central government and shall not receive additional salaries. Article 12: These regulations shall be implemented upon the decision of the Central Executive Committee and Supervisory Committee. (13th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Organizational Regulations for the Qualification Review Committee 53

(Nanjing) The Central Standing Committee held its 66th meeting on the morning of the 13th and approved the Organizational Regulations for the Representative Qualification Review Committee of the Provisional National Congress as follows: Article 1: This committee shall be organized by three members nominated by the Central Executive Committee and two members nominated by the Central Supervisory Committee. Article 2: After each representative registers, they shall immediately submit their party membership card and proof of election to this committee for verification. Article 3: The qualifications of a representative shall be revoked in one of the following circumstances: (1) Does not meet the prescribed qualifications. (2) Has reactionary words or deeds. (3) The election is illegal or fraudulent. Article 4: After the representative's qualification is approved, the committee shall issue a qualification certificate. Article 5: The results of the review shall be reported to the Congress. Article 6: These regulations shall be implemented upon the decision of the Central Executive Committee. (13th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Russo-Japanese Conflict Seems Inevitable

(Harbin) Today, news from Soviet Russia indicates that there are signs of military activity in the Soviet territory near Manchouli. White Russian newspapers speculate that this is a precautionary measure by Soviet Russia, concerned about potential unexpected developments in the railway dispute between "Manchuria" and Russia. Li Shaogeng, the superintendent of the Chinese Eastern Railway, sent a letter to the Soviet authorities requesting the return of locomotives, passenger cars, and freight cars. To date, no official reply has been received. It is rumored that Soviet Russia is only willing to return the freight cars but refuses to return the locomotives. The current state of the Chinese Eastern Railway remains unrestored, and trains are frequently attacked by bandits. It has recently been learned that the tracks near Taipingling were dismantled by bandits, causing a west-bound passenger train to derail at that location. The bandits then opened fire on the train, killing three and injuring many others. (Reuters, 13th)

(Changchun) After the puppet state of "Manchukuo" cut off the Chinese Eastern Railway, the Soviet authorities not only did not stop detaining cars but also demanded that Manchukuo lift the blockade. At the same time, they detain several freight cars daily at the eastern border and transport them through Boli (Khabarovsk) onto the Ussuri Railway, changing their color. As a result, the Chinese Eastern Railway is short of many vehicles, hindering the transportation of goods. The Ministry of Communications of the puppet state of Manchukuo has decided to lodge a serious protest with the Ussuri Railway Bureau, demanding a show of sincerity, or else effective measures will be implemented. (Japanese United Press, 13th)

(Harbin) Chinese Eastern Railway Chairman Koznesov gave the following informal reply to Li Shaogeng, the representative of Manchukuo, regarding the puppet state of "Manchukuo's" final ultimatum yesterday: 600 freight cars have been returned at Manchouli and Pokrani Creek, and more will be returned gradually in the future. However, locomotives are the property of the Soviet Russian Federation, so it is difficult to comply with the request for their return. (Dentsu, 13th)

(Changchun) Because the Soviet side transported various Chinese Eastern Railway cars to Soviet territory, the puppet Manchukuo's Ministry of Communications decisively blocked the connection of vehicles at Manchouli by force. On the 10th, Chinese Eastern Railway Chairman Koznesov issued the following protest to the puppet Manchukuo's Ministry of Communications: "The Manchukuo Ministry of Communications' blockade of the Chinese Eastern Railway at Manchouli has severed connections between the Ussuri and Transbaikal Railways, making transportation impossible. This clearly violates Article 10 of the 1896 regulations for the construction and operation of the Chinese Eastern Railway, and Article 1 of the Russo-Fengtian Agreement also confirmed these old regulations. Therefore, from this perspective, the actions of the Manchukuo Ministry of Communications are a clear violation of the treaty, and it is hoped that the railway blockade will be lifted immediately." (Dentsu, 13th)

(Harbin) Eastern Railway Chairman Koznesov's Economic Talks in Washington Last Night

Eleven Nations Invited to Participate 56

The US Sends Notes, Not Inviting All Nations to Explain

Requests Deliberation Through Normal Diplomatic Channels

Britain, the US, and France Plan to Hold Fireside Chats First

(Washington) It has now been confirmed that the countries specifically invited to participate in the Washington talks are only eleven: France, Britain, Germany, Italy, China, Japan, Argentina, Brazil, Chile, Mexico, and Canada. The other forty-four countries with ambassadors or ministers in Washington will exchange opinions with Secretary of State Hull or, if necessary, with President Roosevelt, through their respective ambassadors or ministers. This morning, the State Department sent notes to each of these countries, requesting that they consult with the United States through diplomatic channels. A personal letter from Hull was also sent simultaneously with the note, explaining that the purpose of this procedure is to save time and stating that the State Department hopes that countries will avoid misunderstandings or incorrect interpretations of the attitude adopted by the United States. (Havas, 12th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt suggested today to hold a fireside chat with British Prime Minister MacDonald and French representative Herriot at the White House. President Roosevelt proposed that visiting heads of government should reside at the White House, while cabinet members should reside at their embassies. Since Herriot is neither a head of government nor a cabinet member, it is widely expected that he will use the French embassy as his residence. Although a round table conference is now out of the question, President Roosevelt is also not opposed to meeting with MacDonald and Herriot simultaneously. According to Roosevelt, it would be good if everyone gathered around the fireplace at the White House. It is reported that several countries have expressed dissatisfaction for not receiving invitations to participate in the Washington talks. The State Department therefore sent letters to the forty-four countries not sending representatives today, inviting their diplomatic representatives to exchange views. (Reuters, 12th)

(Washington) Although the US government has decided to hold separate economic talks with representatives from various countries, there will be one exception. If French representative Herriot arrives in the United States before British Prime Minister MacDonald returns home, President Roosevelt will hold an informal meeting with Herriot before convening a three-way meeting with representatives from Britain and France to discuss various important political issues. Roosevelt believes that Britain, the United States, and France, as democratic countries, should trust and cooperate with each other. He therefore wants to hold a kind of unofficial meeting. Roosevelt previously served as the Brazilian Foreign Minister and US Secretary of State in 1913. Hote, a skilled interpreter fluent in French, will be the translator. (Havas, 13th)

Japan Building Largest Wireless Radio Station, Preparing for Broadcasting War with Nanjing 62

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Communications has decided to build a broadcasting station in Kyushu at a cost of 1 million Japanese yen. When completed, it will be the largest broadcasting station in the Far East. At the same time, it plans to build smaller broadcasting stations in Tokyo and Osaka. (Reuters, 13th)

(Nanjing) Listeners of the Fukuoka Broadcasting Bureau found that the Fukuoka broadcast could not be heard completely and only heard the broadcast from the Nanjing Broadcasting Bureau. After investigation, it was found that the Nanjing Broadcasting Bureau used a wavelength of 667 kilocycles, which was very similar to Fukuoka's 680 kilocycles, resulting in the Japanese broadcast being interfered with by the Nanjing broadcast. Therefore, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is protesting to the Nanjing side based on international law regarding wireless radio. Although the Chinese side replied that it would change the wavelength, there is no prospect of it being realized. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications plans to counter this by building a 100-kilowatt broadcasting station to launch a broadcasting war with Nanjing. (Dentsu, 13th)

Notification of Abolition of Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty, Major Blow to Dumping of Japanese Goods 65

Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs Sends Instructions to Matsudaira

Requests the British Government to Relax Tariffs

(Nanjing) The British government has notified Japan that the Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty will expire and be abolished in October of this year. Yesterday afternoon, as a result of discussions by Vice Minister Arida and Director of the Bureau of Commerce Kurisu, it was agreed that although Japan could not request the withdrawal of the notification according to the provisions of the treaty, the result, whether it was the abolition of the most-favored-nation treatment or the imposition of high anti-dumping duties on Japanese exports, would be undesirable for Indo-Japanese trade and for the feelings of the Japanese people towards Britain. It was decided to request the British government to reconsider based on this view. Yesterday, instructions to the following effect were sent to Matsudaira, the ambassador to Britain: (1) The Japanese government will endeavor to ensure self-respect among industry players and export controls; (2) After the abolition of the commercial treaty, drastic taxation should not be imposed solely on Japanese exports; (3) Exports such as three-in-one soil do not threaten the Indian market and must be exempted from anti-dumping duties and continue to be granted most-favored-nation treatment as before. (Dentsu, 13th)

Advocating the Principle of Freedom of Commerce, Planning to Strive for It at the Washington Conference 67

(Nanjing) According to the Japanese Foreign Ministry spokesperson, the Japanese government plans to vigorously advocate the principle of freedom of commerce at the Washington Conference and oppose countries raising tariffs on Japanese goods and imposing anti-dumping duties. The content of the so-called principle of freedom of commerce is: (1) Cancellation of exceptions to the most-favored-nation clause, such as the British Ottawa Agreement; (2) Tariffs should be based on mutual benefit between the two countries; (3) Protective tariffs should be negotiated through diplomatic means and implemented after mutual understanding is reached; (4) Removal of tariff barriers. Pan-American Day: Roosevelt's Important Speech 88

Strongly Argues for the Necessity of Overcoming Trade Barriers in the Americas

Frequent War Disasters in South America Set Back Civilization

国民 Twelve Washington dispatch: Today was one of the busiest days for US President Roosevelt since the end of the banking crisis. He went to the board of directors of the Association of American Republics in the morning to give a speech. As today is Pan-American Day, Roosevelt took the opportunity to strongly argue for the necessity of overcoming man-made trade barriers in the Americas. Previously, Latin American countries had launched the most fierce criticism of the US tariff act, and Roosevelt had also acknowledged that high tariffs hindered trade between the United States and South American countries. Therefore, at today's speech, he first announced that the time had come to overcome trade barriers and allow the goods of each other to flow back and forth on a fair and beneficial basis. One of the most difficult problems between the United States and various South American countries is overproduction. For example, the United States and Argentina both have large surpluses of wheat, while Brazil is saddened by surpluses of coffee. All urgently need to seek smooth trade.

Reuters Washington telegram: President Roosevelt, in his speech commemorating Pan-American Day, stated that the undeclared wars between Bolivia and Paraguay and between Chile and Peru are acts of regression. The governments of the Americas should each take the initiative as soon as possible to completely abolish all unnecessary and man-made barriers that hinder the commercial prosperity between the peoples of the American republics.

US Plan to Save Military Spending: Hagood Explains to Congress 89

国民 Twelve Washington dispatch: Major General Hagood stated to the US House of Representatives Army Committee today on a plan for national defense and saving military expenses, saying that it had been submitted to the White House for a long time, but the President neither approved nor rejected it. Hagood was summoned to the House for consultations on opinions on saving military expenses, and immediately stated the urgent need for suitable defense on both the land and sea. His plan (1) would abolish the Philippine patrol force; (2) withdraw all land armies stationed in China; (3) US coastal artillery units and field artillery units should be merged into a single military unit; (4) Add to the naval defenses of each port to reach pre-war strength; (5) Continue building warships to at least match the strongest navy in the world; (6) Abolish dozens of military agencies to streamline administrative procedures; (7) Make the Reserve Officers' Training Corps the foundation of the national defense system. Hagood firmly believes that there is no need to station a land army in China today, and since the Philippines has an independence bill, it should be allowed to train its own land army. As for the Philippine patrol force, its nature is equivalent to the national defense team stationed in each state within the United States, except that the patrol force is a paid army, with more than 6,000 soldiers on duty year-round, all of whom are Filipinos, and most of the officers are Americans. Military salaries are paid by the US central government. According to Hagood's estimate, after abolishing useless teams and streamlining roundabout procedures, 50 million yuan in military expenses can be saved annually, with no impact on strength.

In 1929, she was elected as a member of the 71st and 72nd Congresses. She is currently 57 years old. Her husband, who served as a Major in the British Army's Royal Engineers, has passed away. Continued Trial of British Engineers in Moscow 92

Reuter, Moscow, 12th: One of the most intriguing cases in history continued this afternoon in the Blue Hall of the Trade Union Building in Moscow.

The indictment, in which the Soviet Union accuses six British engineers of committing the following five crimes: (1) belonging to a counter-revolutionary party; (2) collecting secret military and civilian information; (3) participating in sabotage activities; (4) bribing Russian engineers and workers to exchange for espionage and sabotage work; (5) bribing Russian engineers to cover up defects in the installation of the Wickers Company equipment. The document is seventy-seven pages long and was read aloud this morning.

The defendant, Macdonald, confessed to his guilt, while the other five British engineers pleaded not guilty. The indictment alleges that Macdonald confessed to engaging in espionage activities under the instructions of Thornton and Monkhouse. The evidence presented this morning was based entirely on the confessions of the defendants after their arrest on March 12 and the reports of the Soviet Expert Committee's investigation of certain documents.

During the resumption of the hearing in the afternoon, the first witness was a Russian named Gusev, who had red hair and a trembling voice. He was questioned by Russian prosecutor Vyshinsky. Gusev claimed that he belonged to the White Army and began counter-revolutionary work after meeting with Wickers Company employees in 1929. He was instructed by Macdonald to provide information about the factory, especially focusing on military installations and the types of shells they manufactured. After speaking, Gusev left the witness stand.

In the silent atmosphere, the prosecutor called Macdonald to the stand and questioned him, saying, "Is it true that you know Gusev?" Macdonald replied, "Yes, we were good friends in 1930." The prosecutor asked, "Why did you instruct him to provide information?" Macdonald answered, "I did it for my own purposes." Macdonald's calm and composed tone aroused the emotions of the courtroom observers. The judge quickly rang the bell to instruct the audience to maintain order and remain silent. Gusev then took the stand again to provide a detailed account of how he sabotaged machinery and sought information, stating that he placed metallic objects in the machinery at the Slato-Ustes Electric Plant and that Macdonald was aware of this plan. At this point, the prosecutor turned to Macdonald and asked, "Is this true?" Macdonald replied, "Yes, it is true." Macdonald also admitted to giving Gusev 3,500 rubles. Gusev continued to say that he used go-slow tactics to delay production at the Slato-Ustes Electric Plant. However, Macdonald said he knew nothing about this. Gusev also stated that the purpose of the go-slow tactics was to harm the efficiency of the Soviet military. When he served in other power plants, he introduced other employees to Macdonald, and Macdonald recommended him to Thornton as someone who could provide information. Thornton, hearing this testimony, expressed indignation. Gusev continued, saying that after Macdonald left Slato-Ustes, they corresponded under assumed names, and the intermediary was a woman named Li Bofa. Macdonald also ordered Wickers Company secretary Gadusov to send instructions to Gusev, but not using Gusev's real name. After hearing this testimony, Macdonald looked down and, in answering the prosecutor's questions, said that he had sent letters to Gusev, but it was for company matters and not to instruct him to provide information. At this point, the prosecutor wanted to prove that Thornton was aware that Gusev was engaged in espionage activities under Macdonald's instructions, so he called Thornton to the stand. Thornton claimed that he met Gusev in a tavern in the Ural Mountains.

After speaking for about an hour, he began to discuss the proposals. The important figures also had important proposals, mainly including: joint suppression by provinces in connecting areas, security of the coast and hinterland of the Yangtze River during the resistance against Japan and suppression of communists, organization and training of people's defense corps and baojia system, allocation of troops and defense works in various places, and rectification and training of troops. The meeting continued in the afternoon and was scheduled to last for two days, depending on the number of proposals. It is heard that the generals have been discussing military affairs related to resisting Japan and suppressing communists with Chiang in Jiangxi for several days, and they are willing to be at the forefront of the resistance against Japan. Concrete and detailed measures have been discussed regarding the transfer of elite troops from various units to the north for combat and the increase of troops into Jiangxi to eliminate Zhu Mao within a limited time. The generals will return to their defenses after the military meeting closes because of the importance of defense. (April 11)

Control Yuan Impeaches Wei Daoming 100

Enumerates Facts of Bribery and Illegal Acts

Requests the Government to Impose Disciplinary Action According to Law

Control Committee member Shao Hongji has proposed the impeachment of former Nanjing Mayor Wei Daoming for accepting bribes, engaging in corruption, violating laws, and dereliction of duty in the handling of the Nanjing water pipe project, as well as for forging receipts and embezzling funds with former Finance Bureau chiefs Qi Xu, Wang Renlin, and Cheng Yuanfan. The Control Yuan has issued the case to Control Committee members Xiong Yuxi and others for investigation, which has been confirmed. They have submitted a request to the National Government to forward it to the Committee for the Punishment of Political Officials for handling according to law. The original proposal and investigation report are listed below.

Control Yuan Submission 101

Regarding the matter of submission, according to the impeachment by Control Committee member Shao Hongji against former Nanjing Mayor Wei Daoming for accepting bribes, engaging in corruption, violating laws, and dereliction of duty, the Control Yuan has assigned Control Committee members Xiong Yuxi, Zheng Lusheng, and Yang Pusheng to investigate. Now, according to the report, it is believed that disciplinary action should be taken. Therefore, the original case documents are copied and submitted to the Government for review and forwarded to the Committee for the Punishment of Political Officials for handling, which would be for the public convenience. Sincerely submitted to Lin, Chairman of the National Government, including a copy of the original impeachment document, a copy of the original investigation report, Yu Youren, President of the Control Yuan.

Original Impeachment Document 102

Regarding the matter of proposal, it is found that the capital city has been operating the waterworks for nearly two years. Citizens are eager to release the water as soon as possible to emphasize hygiene. Last month, when the main pipeline was just installed and the water pressure was tested, water pipe bursts were repeatedly discovered, indicating that the quality of the materials was poor. It is rumored that the person in charge of purchasing materials贪图回扣and engaged in corruption, involving four to fifty hundred thousand yuan. Committee member Shao Hongji feared that the rumors might not be credible, so he went to the Municipal Government to review the files and secretly investigated separately. Now, the identified doubts are recorded as follows: (1) The contract for water pipes and accessories was signed in April of the 20th year of the Republic of China by former Nanjing Mayor Wei Daoming with the Shanghai Paris Industrial Electrical Factory, the agent of the French德蒙松铁厂. An order was placed for a batch of water pipes and accessories, totaling US$350,000, half in cash and half in promissory notes. The promissory notes were also specified in the appendix to the contract to be exchanged for US$6,000 per month, starting from January 30th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, and exchanged in order for 30 months (estimated to be exchanged in full by July 30th of the 22nd year of the Republic of China). Unexpectedly, before February of the 21st year of the Republic of China, former Mayor Wei Daoming had already exchanged US$75,000 in cash, and only a balance of US$1,785 remains. It is found that the intention of the above installment payments was to limit the speed of delivery. If there was a delay, the fine would be deducted from this payment. The Mayor did not wait for the order to be delivered in full, nor did he make the payments monthly. Instead, he prepaid all the payments before the due date, which obviously involves other circumstances. This is a point of suspicion. (2) The contract stipulates that the delivery period should be before October 10th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, and that all goods should be delivered to the designated location (Nanjing) in three installments, with a fine of US$200 per day for delays. It is found that the factory shipped in nine batches. The first six batches were delivered on time. The last three batches were delivered one month late. In addition, some accessories have not been delivered and have not responded to repeated reminders, resulting in delayed installation. It is found that the contract clearly stipulates penalties for delays. Mayor Wei Daoming did not perform the penalties as stipulated in the contract. He did not deduct the unpaid payments but issued promissory notes in advance, which is incomprehensible. This is the second point of suspicion. (3) Once the installed water pipes were tested with water pressure, more than 30 of them burst. It is found that there are many pinholes in the delivered water pipes and accessories. Not only is the quality of the materials poor, but the thinnest part of the burst water pipes, as examined by the Bureau of Public Works, is only more than 13 millimeters, which differs by 15% from the original contract specification of 16 millimeters. The factory relies on the fact that the payments have been received and there is no guarantee, so it delays in replacing and compensating. Who should be held responsible for this? This is the third point of suspicion. (4) After reading the contract for ordering water pipes and accessories, "Article 13. Bank Guarantee: Within 10 days after signing the contract, Party B (the factory) shall provide a bank guarantee acceptable to Party A (the government) to fulfill all the conditions of this contract." It is found that there is only an original English letter from the factory and a draft in the original file, and no formal guarantee. Therefore, the factory does not perform the contract, and our Municipal Government has repeatedly failed to respond to reminders. The public has suffered considerable losses as a result. Who should be held responsible for this? Furthermore, it is rumored that Mayor Wei withdrew a formal guarantee certificate from a certain bank before leaving office and returned it to the factory after receiving a bribe. This is not without cause. This is the fourth point of suspicion. In summary of the above-mentioned facts, it is found that former Nanjing Mayor Wei Daoming (a student who studied in France) did not use the bidding method for all water pipes, and the materials ordered were not only of poor quality but also did not meet the thickness specified in the original contract. The water pipes and other items were delayed in delivery, and instead, the payments were prepaid. It is no wonder that the citizens slander him. The most important thing is that the bank guarantee certificate for Party B to fulfill this contract was privately withdrawn, only seeking to enrich himself and disregarding the rights of the public. His bribery, corruption, violation of law, and dereliction of duty are obvious. Therefore, an impeachment is filed according to law, requesting that former Nanjing Mayor Wei Daoming be immediately transferred for disciplinary action, that his criminal part be handed over to the court for strict interrogation, and that he be ordered to compensate for public losses to maintain official integrity and serve as a warning to those who are greedy. This is submitted to the Dean for review and implementation. Shao Hongji, Inspector. (To be continued)

Li Liejun Sends Telegram to Central Party Headquarters Arguing for Freedom Guarantees 106

Central Committee member Li Liejun sent a telegram to the Central Party Headquarters the day before yesterday, requesting that an order be issued to all party, government, and military organs across the country to implement guarantees of freedom of assembly, association, speech, and publication. The original telegram read: "Respectfully to the Central Party Headquarters: Since the Central Executive Committee decided on March 30th to convene a temporary representative assembly and discuss the early convening of the National Assembly, the general public has felt that there is still a glimmer of hope for the political future. To realize this hope, since the Central Committee has decided to make the government open and gather the wisdom of the people to jointly decide on national affairs, it should first demonstrate sincerity to the world. This is what the people desire, and this is what the government should strive for. Therefore, the freedom of assembly, association, speech, and publication for the people, which has been declared repeatedly, should not be reduced to empty words again. Otherwise, if the people cannot even assemble and cannot even speak, how can they contribute their wisdom, let alone save the country? On the 5th of this month, the two proposed measures by Committee Member Wang Jingwei in response to Committee Member Soong Ching-ling's proposal, although they do not fully satisfy the people's desires, seem fair and just in discussing the matter. However, the key is to be able to implement things, and for the top and bottom to be of one mind and the whole country to be united. If the Central Committee has a plan to start anew with the people, but the party and government officials in the various provinces and cities do not conscientiously obey orders, how can they demonstrate the Central Committee's impartiality to the world? Today's difficulties are extreme. To save the country from danger, we must first revitalize ourselves. We should follow the lessons of Duke Xiao of Qin, who did not compromise in the face of adversity and adopted good advice, and the courage of Goujian of Yue, who avenged Wu. We should resolutely and thoroughly seek progress. Then, with sincere intentions, there will be a response from all quarters. I believe that at this time, the Central Committee should issue an order to all party, government, and military organs across the country, making its intentions clear, so that the enlightened will be encouraged and the uninformed will be relieved. In this way, a new, open approach can quickly achieve significant results. I respectfully submit this and hope for your consideration and acceptance." Li Liejun respectfully bows.

Mrs. Sun knew that Huang was under surveillance and had lost his freedom of speech, so she said goodbye and left.

American Military Aircraft Demonstration Performed at Longhua Yesterday Morning 108

Latest Model, High Speed and Large Size

Piloted by an American Aviation Major

The Flying Eagle single-engine military aircraft of the China Aviation Transport Company, the latest product from the United States, arrived in Shanghai a few days ago. At 10 a.m. yesterday morning, a public demonstration was held at Longhua Airport. It was piloted by Major Du Lide, a world-renowned aviator from the United States who recently arrived in Shanghai. Those who attended included the newly appointed Governor of the Central Bank, Kong Xiangxi, Kong's secretary Xu Jianping, Director of the Consolidated Tobacco Tax Bureau Xie Qi, and dozens of Chinese and foreign journalists. The China National Aviation Corporation made prior arrangements, and the Public Security Bureau dispatched police and airline staff to maintain order on site.

Exquisite Technique 109

The aircraft is a biplane single-seat military aircraft. The wings are painted yellow and the fuselage is dark gray. At 10:30 a.m., Major Du Lide began to prepare to board the aircraft. As soon as the engine started, the aircraft took off and first circled the field several times, then flew high into the clouds, performing all kinds of extremely dangerous maneuvers, such as flying upside down, sideways, spinning like a windmill, or skimming over the heads of the audience, all of which were extremely skillful. The audience was full of admiration. The performance lasted for half an hour before landing at the airport.

American Aviator Du Lide

Instructs on Construction 110

After Major Du Lide disembarked, Kong Xiangxi and others stepped forward to shake his hand. Then Du gave a detailed explanation of the aircraft's construction, saying that this aircraft is the latest product of the United States this year, and has all kinds of attack and defense equipment. The nose is equipped with a machine gun, and 12 heavy bombs can be placed under the wings. Its engine is a Wright rotary eagle type, with 650 horsepower, but can be increased to 700 horsepower. The cruising speed is 245 miles per hour, and it can fly as high as 35,000 feet. Kong and others were all satisfied and left happily.

Worth Over 300,000 111

Yesterday, this reporter interviewed Major Du Lide. According to him, this aircraft has two major advantages: flexible maneuverability, high speed and large size, and convenient landing. Each aircraft currently costs more than 80,000 US dollars, which is equivalent to more than 300,000 Chinese dollars. The highest altitude of today's performance was only 3,000 feet.

Du's History 112

Joined the United States Army Air Service Reserve in 1917. During the European War, he served as a training officer for pursuit, combat, and shooting skills. From 1919 to 1921, he served in the US-Mexico border air patrol. The following year, he made the first non-stop flight across the American continent, achieving it in less than 24 hours, setting a new record in the aviation industry. Later, he was in charge of the Army aircraft testing affairs at McCook Airfield. He won the international Schneider Trophy competition in Baltimore with a speed of 232 miles per hour. Since 1926, he has been performing abroad with American-made aircraft. In 1930, he resigned from the military and joined the American Hacker Oil Company. Last year, he set a new world record for land aircraft with a speed of 294.43 miles per hour.

Japanese Consulate Replies with Evasions Regarding the Li Chunshan Case 114

Suspect Transferred to Court

City Government Will Negotiate Again

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the case of the kidnapping of Korean national Li Chunshan on Luban Road, the city government, considering that the case occurred in the Chinese territory, ordered the Municipal Public Security Bureau to strictly arrest the kidnappers. After interrogation, the Municipal Public Security Bureau arrested a suspect named Diao Degao, who confessed that he was following the instructions of Japanese nationals Yamada and Kato to kidnap him. A few days after the incident, the local North-China Daily News reported that Li Chunshan had been escorted back to Korea by police from the Japanese Consulate in Shanghai. The city government considered the circumstances of this matter to be serious, so it sent a letter to the Japanese Consul General Ishii, requesting him to investigate and reply. Yesterday, the Japanese Consulate replied to the city government with content that was entirely evasive. Yesterday, the reporter visited Secretary-General Yu Hongjun of the city government and asked about the future negotiation policy. I was kindly informed in detail. The Japanese Consul General's reply and Secretary-General Yu's statement are recorded below.

Japanese Consul General's Reply: "To the Esteemed Mayor Wu: Regarding the case of the kidnapping of a Korean person Li Chunshan on March 9th of this year, I acknowledge receipt of your letter No. 1831 of April 8th, stating that the case has been investigated and found to have been committed by Japanese nationals Yamada and Kato, and requesting that these two individuals be arrested and brought to justice. The Consulate General has not been informed of this case, and the Japanese nationals mentioned in the letter have only surnames and no names. Therefore, it is difficult for this Consulate to investigate the facts. I hereby reply and request your review." Ishii Jotaro, Japanese Consul General in Shanghai.

Yu's Statement: According to Secretary-General Yu Hongjun of the city government, since the Li Chunshan kidnapping case occurred, the city government believes that since Li Chunshan has become a naturalized Korean, he should be protected by Chinese law, and the incident occurred in Chinese territory. Therefore, the Municipal Public Security Bureau was immediately ordered to strictly arrest the kidnappers. A suspect named Diao Degao was arrested, who confessed that he was kidnapped by Japanese nationals Yamada and others. Later, the local North-China Daily News reported that Li Chunshan had been escorted back to Korea by police from the Japanese Consulate. The city government immediately inquired with the Japanese Consulate, which replied that it was impossible to investigate because there were only surnames and no names, without denying the news reported in the North-China Daily News. In addition to ordering the Municipal Public Security Bureau to send the suspect Diao to the local court for legal proceedings, the city government also sent a letter to the local court, requesting that Diao be thoroughly interrogated to clarify the truth. At the same time, the Municipal Public Security Bureau was ordered to continue investigating the case and provide a concrete reply so that further negotiations could be conducted with the Japanese side.

Indian Sikh Community Celebrates the Five Heroes Memorial 116

According to the Continental Daily News, Indian Sikhs around the world are celebrating the birth of the Sikh Union, also known as the Sikh New Year, today (the 13th). The Sikh community in Shanghai began celebrating at midnight yesterday (the 12th) with a grand ceremony at the Indian Temple at 330 Baoshan Road, with many attendees. The celebration commemorates the heroic deeds of the five leaders and Xinji, the founder of Sikhism. A special event will be held at the temple again from 2 p.m. to 5 p.m. today (the 13th), and people from other countries are invited to participate. There will be feasts and celebrations throughout the day. Today marks the anniversary of the Sikhs' liberation from Muslim oppression. It is said that in 1696 AD, the tenth Sikh leader Xinji convened a conference to commemorate his ancestors. 50,000 believers gathered, including Nanakji, who had dedicated his life to propagating opposition to Muslim oppression. He spoke to the crowd, asking them to sympathize with the suffering of their compatriots and work together to rescue them. Then the tenth Xinji asked the believers for five heads to wash away the filth of the Muslim king's tyranny with their blood. Five people immediately stepped forward, willing to sacrifice themselves for their compatriots. These five people did not lose their heads but became leaders of the Sikh community. The people were moved by the heroic deeds of these five people and united to achieve liberation.

Results of the Collision Between the Deli and Haiguang Vessels 118

Deli Loses Over 5,000 Taels

One Passenger Dead, One Injured

The Deli vessel, belonging to the Zhejiang Shipping Company, located at No. 1 Hengxin Lane, Nanshi, collided with the Haiguang oil tanker of the Asiatic Petroleum Company at 9 p.m. on the 11th of last month in the waters of Yangshan. The Deli vessel was damaged, and one passenger died. The details are recorded below.

Collision Situation: The Zhejiang Company's Deli vessel operates on the Shanghai-Haimen-Dinghai-Huangyan route. This time, it was returning to Shanghai from Huangyan. It departed from Dinghai on the morning of the 11th. Around 9 p.m., when it reached the waters of Yangshan, it saw the Haiguang vessel approaching rapidly. Its course was wrong and the distance was about one nautical mile. The Deli immediately sounded a warning. The Haiguang replied with one blast, but the vessel did not turn aside and continued straight ahead. The Deli then sounded another warning and turned its rudder to starboard to avoid danger. Unexpectedly, the distance was too short. As a result, the stern of the vessel, on the port side, and the second-class cabin were hit by the bow of the Haiguang vessel, creating a hole. An iron anchor from the port side of the Haiguang vessel was embedded in the iron plate, and the anchor chain was broken. Fortunately, it was above the waterline, so it was still possible to sail to Shanghai.

One Dead, One Injured: The vessel was carrying passengers and goods from Huangyan, Dinghai, and other places to Shanghai, with fresh eggs being the main cargo. There were more than 120 passengers in total. When the Haiguang collided with the vessel, a person from Taizhou named Luo Qihan, around 50 years old, was sleeping on the fresh eggs in the area where the hole was created. When the iron anchor broke through the iron plate and entered the vessel, it struck Luo's head, crushing it and causing the brain to spill out. The scene was too terrible to witness, and he died immediately. Another person nearby was hit in the head by iron debris and was slightly injured. After the vessel arrived in Shanghai, it reported the incident to the court for inspection. The body was temporarily placed in the Taizhou Guild Hall. A telegram was sent to Dinghai to inquire about Luo's family and notify them to come to Shanghai to claim the body. The matter of compensation will be discussed separately.

Yili Rescue: After the Deli was hit, it sounded a distress call. Fortunately, the Yili vessel of the Yili Company, which had departed from Dinghai as well, was behind it. After hearing the distress call, the Yili vessel quickly approached the Deli and completely rescued the passengers. The Deli then made some minor repairs and sailed to Shanghai.

A Glimpse of the Losses: The vessel has a deadweight of over 700 tons. This time, it was returning to Shanghai from Huangyan, carrying mainly fresh eggs. The collision with the Haiguang vessel damaged four iron plates and several rooms in the upper-deck cabin. The iron railings on the port side were broken, and 51 baskets of fresh eggs were damaged. The total loss is estimated at around 5,000 taels.

Inspection and Negotiation: Fortunately, the hole was above the waterline on the port side. The iron anchor of the Haiguang vessel is still embedded in the iron plate of the Deli. The rudder of the vessel was also slightly damaged. Afterwards, the shipowner made repairs and sailed to Shanghai, arriving at around 8 a.m. on the 12th. After unloading the cargo, it sailed to the waters off Longhua and anchored. The shipowner reported the collision to the company. The company had received news from the Yili vessel. After receiving the report from this vessel, it immediately reported to the relevant authorities and sent a letter to the Asiatic Petroleum Company to negotiate. It also sent a letter to the insurance company. Yesterday afternoon around 2 p.m., the Asiatic Petroleum Company sent a Westerner and an employee of the insurance company to the vessel along with representatives from the company to conduct an inspection. It is said that the responsibility for the incident lies with the Haiguang vessel. The Haiguang vessel was carrying kerosene to Ningbo and is expected to arrive in Shanghai today. After the Deli is inspected, it will be repaired at that location.

Automatic Telephone Service of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications to Begin Operation at Midnight Tomorrow 119

Can Communicate with the Concessions for Long Distance

User Billing and Usage Method

The automatic telephone service of the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications will begin operation at midnight on the 15th of this month. Details of the billing and usage method for long-distance calls with the concessions are as follows: (1) "Payment of Deposit": Any user who wishes to call a user in the concessions must first pay a deposit of 5 yuan to the Shanghai Telephone Bureau. (2) "Usage Method": When a user wants to make a call to the concessions, after confirming and noting the other party's number, pick up the receiver. After hearing the "buzzing" sound, dial 0. After an operator answers, state the other party's user number in sequence and wait for the call to connect. (3) "Calculation of Calls": The standard for counting calls starts from the time both parties start talking. Every three minutes is counted as one call (even if it is less than three minutes, it is counted as one call). Each call costs 5 cents. If the call time exceeds three minutes, it is counted as two calls. If it exceeds six minutes, it is counted as three calls, and so on. (4) "For Long Distance Calls": Users who wish to make long-distance calls must first pay a deposit of 10 yuan. (5) "Usage Method": You can dial 40. However, it may take some time for long-distance calls to connect. Before the called user answers, you must wait for the connection and do not leave, it is said.

The City Council Disaster Area Reconstruction Group Met Yesterday 121

Drafting Regulations and Urging the City Government to Actively Proceed

In order to promote the reconstruction of the disaster area as soon as possible, the Shanghai Provisional City Council had previously appointed councilors Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Chen Bingqian, Wang Yiting, Du Yuesheng, Li Fuxun, and Xu Yongzuo as members to be specifically in charge of this matter, and designated Xu Yongzuo to convene meetings, as reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday, the members met at the Bank Club. Except for Wang Xiaolai and Du Yuesheng, who were out of Shanghai due to other engagements, all members attended. It was decided to name the group the City Council Disaster Area Reconstruction Group, formulate the group's regulations, and unanimously decide to send a letter to the City Council to regularly invite representatives from the city government to attend meetings, explain the reconstruction plan and its implementation status, in order to emphasize municipal administration. The proposals and regulations of the group, as well as the original letter requesting the city government to send representatives to attend the meeting and explain the situation, are recorded below.

Meeting Situation 122

The Disaster Area Reconstruction Group of the Shanghai Provisional City Council held its first meeting at the Bank Club on Hong Kong Road at noon on April 13th. Councilors Yu Qiaqing, Chen Bingqian, Wang Yiting, Li Fuxun, and Xu Yongzuo attended. Wang Xiaolai and Du Yuesheng were absent.

Resolutions 123

The following matters were discussed: (1) The Name of the Group. Xu Yongzuo reported that the City Council had previously appointed the seven of them to be specifically responsible for reviewing and supervising the reconstruction of the city's disaster area, and had named it the Shanghai City Reconstruction Disaster Area Design Committee. The group should discuss and decide whether the name is appropriate. He also designated himself as the convener of the meeting. He believed that the name of the above committee was likely to cause two misunderstandings: (1) it has the suspicion of interfering with administration, and (2) it seems to be an independent and external organization, which is not in line with the powers of the City Council and the internal organization. Therefore, it is proposed to refer to the regulations of the City Council's organizational rules for grouping the Fourth Article, named the Disaster Area Reconstruction Group, its name implies that it is purely an internal review agency of the City Council, shall not exercise powers to the outside, so the name can be corrected to avoid misunderstandings, can you ask for a resolution? After public discussion, it was unanimously approved. (2) The Group's Regulations. Xu Yongzuo drafted the group's regulations and distributed them to the councilors for circulation. After public discussion, the original draft was passed without modification, and it was resolved to submit it to the City Council for discussion and implementation. (3) Implementation Methods. Xu Yongzuo proposed that the original intention of the City Council in establishing this group was to promote the early completion of the reconstruction of the disaster area. In order to follow this purpose, the group must first understand the city government's reconstruction plan and its implementation procedures, otherwise it would be impossible to proceed. It has been four months since the issuance of the 6 million yuan reconstruction bonds, but the disaster area still shows broken tiles and ruined walls, and the desolation is full of eyes, the citizens' expectations for reconstruction are no less than the hope of clouds and rainbows in a great drought, the city government has really proceeded to what extent, it is very suspenseful, it is proposed that this group write to the City Council to convene a regular meeting, and ask the city government to send representatives to attend and explain in detail, now draw up a letter to the City Council, if everyone agrees, then please sign and seal it, after the public read the letter, they unanimously agreed, and signed and sealed it on the spot and sent it to the City Council, the meeting was adjourned.

City Chamber of Commerce Letter to Fish Trade Groups Urging Strict Enforcement of Regulations and Ceasing Sale of Japanese Fish 125

Unscrupulous Merchants Repeatedly Sell Japanese Fish Due to Greed

Trade Associations Should Restrain Members from Covertly Violating Regulations

Yesterday, the City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to both the Ice-Chilled Fish Trade Association and the Salted Fish Trade Association, urging them to restrain their members from importing Japanese fish. The original letter stated: "We have received a letter from the Fish Trade Inspection Committee for Enemy Goods stating that despite our repeated resistance against Japanese oppression and our attempts to boycott goods, we have ultimately failed. The reasons for this failure are twofold: (1) The officials are not diligent and engage in favoritism and corruption. (2) The inspectors lack the experience to distinguish enemy goods. In the past, the merchant organization had an Economic Relations with Japan Committee, which believed that each trade had personnel capable of identifying enemy goods, making it easier to eliminate them. However, this initiative was hampered by two factors: first, accusations from the outside that merchants were protecting each other, and second, committee members of trade associations being irresponsible and prioritizing personal relationships. Since the September 18th Incident, our fish trade has largely relied on Russian merchants for imported fish, such as salmon. However, recently, a small number of unscrupulous merchants have openly transported Japanese Busan Daechongcheon Donggukou dried oiled fresh fish without any scruples. Daechongcheon goods are similar to those from Vladivostok, and oiled fresh fish are similar to American small fresh fish. Although outsiders cannot distinguish these goods, many within the fish trade also cannot identify them. In light of this, we have urgently established this association to identify the source of enemy goods, down to a single box. For example, the recent shipment of 932 boxes of Daechongcheon goods, which unscrupulous merchants intended to sell, was diverted to Qingdao due to our association's surveillance. Selling this cargo in Shanghai would have yielded several thousand yuan in profit, while exporting it would have resulted in a loss of one thousand yuan. In the future, our association will not only prevent the sale of enemy goods but also secretly inform anti-Japanese associations in various locations to detain and severely punish offenders. As for the issue of Japanese vessels intruding on our fishing grounds, we must resist them even more strongly. These fresh fish are managed by companies such as the Kyodo Kabushiki Gaisha Nikko Yoko, which specifically entrusts the distribution to fishmongers in Xiaodongmen. However, most fishmongers in Xiaodongmen have refused to sell them due to significant debts owed to boat owners, with only Qiafeng Gongshun and a few other shops agreeing to sell them. After our association was established, we sent a warning letter to the Ice-Chilled Fish Association. However, Qiafeng Fish Shop and Shenfeng Yongmao Fruit Shop have continued to sell them without any hesitation. Yesterday, our association received a report that the Daicheng Maru had arrived with 1,200 boxes of small yellow croaker. At 3:00 AM, our executives, Jin Chuxiang and Huang Zenshi, led the entire staff to the location and seized the cargo. Qiafeng Shop and Shenfeng Yongmao Fruit Shop were selling the fish. In addition to urging them to stop selling, we also lectured the peddlers on the dangers of Japanese fishing encroachment. The audience was outraged and poured kerosene on the fish, which slightly deterred the unscrupulous merchants. Today, all enemy fish sales have been suspended. However, we fear that unscrupulous merchants, driven by greed, may attempt to sell them covertly again. Our association plans to take further action. We pledge, with an honest and impartial conscience, to sacrifice everything to eliminate enemy fish. Our association is organized through the cooperation of workers and managers, who supervise each other to achieve fairness and integrity. We are eager to report our work progress at any time and hope that your association will instruct all trades in this city to conduct the same movement to facilitate the boycott of goods. We would be deeply grateful for your guidance." The letter emphasizes that ceasing the sale of Japanese fish is essential for economic severance with Japan. Since the provisional members' meeting of this association on September 20th, we have repeatedly emphasized this matter. Based on the previous situation, it is evident that the association's regulations have not been strictly enforced, leading to increasingly lax prohibitions, which is regrettable. To learn from past mistakes, your association should make every effort to revitalize itself, restrain its members, and prevent them from superficially complying while covertly violating regulations, as this would damage the association's credibility. This is of utmost importance.

Wang Fushen's Private Wireless Telephone Invention Amid National Crisis 128

Results of Trials at the Central Research Institute in the Capital

Extremely Suitable for Military Orders and Superior to Encrypted Telegrams

The Institute of Physics Sends Personnel to Shanghai for Further Trials

Wang Fushen, a student at the National Tongji University in Wusong, has recently invented a type of private wireless telephone. After discussions with the Minister of Education, Zhu Jiahua, and the Director of the Telegraph Administration, Yan Renguang, and trials at the Central Research Institute, the invention is considered extremely suitable for all military command and order purposes in the current national crisis, and even superior to the currently used military cipher telegrams in terms of secrecy. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency specifically drove to the university yesterday to interview Wang regarding the invention's development. The following is a record of what he was told:

Motivation for Invention 129

According to Wang, "Several years ago, I noticed that military telegrams, even with encryption, were sometimes easily deciphered, and the risk was even greater if the codebook was lost. At that time, the idea of researching wireless telephone arose in my mind. However, it was very complicated at first, and due to economic reasons, I was unable to conduct sufficient research, so the matter was temporarily shelved."

After the January 28th Incident 130

"When the January 28th Shanghai Incident occurred last year, our school was devastated by the Japanese army. Overcome with pain and anger, the idea of the secret wireless telephone in my mind suddenly reappeared, so I actively researched it. By October, I realized that the machine's structure was extremely simple. At that time, I discussed the idea with my classmate, Li Jisun, who believed that it was worth trying. So, I implored the school authorities to provide financial assistance, and as a result, I was granted permission by Principal Weng Zilong and Secretary-General Zhou Shang to conduct the experiment."

Successful Trial 131

"Subsequently, the Institute of Physics of the Central Research Institute discussed it and Mr. Cai Jintao came to the school in person to re-test it, believing that the theory and facts were consistent, with only a small part remaining to be improved. This small part is very easy to improve and will be modified in the near future to make it perfect."

Audience with Zhu in the Capital 132

"After the successful trial, I went to Beijing to meet with the Minister of Education, Zhu Jiahua, through the introduction of Principal Weng Zilong. I was granted an audience, and I presented the origin and development of the private wireless telephone to Mr. Zhu. Afterwards, I was introduced by Minister Zhu to Yan Renguang, the Director of the Telegraph Administration of the Ministry of Communications. When I met Mr. Yan, in addition to explaining the principles and asking for his corrections (because Mr. Yan is a radio expert), I also asked whether it could be offered for military use. Mr. Yan listened and replied that it could, so he ordered me to go to the National Defense Design Committee to meet with Zhu Qiqing, a full-time committee member. At the same time, he also invited another specialist, Jin Xianzao, to meet with me. After a long discussion, both Mr. Jin and Mr. Zhu hoped that I would quickly submit a formal request for military authorities to adopt it."

Better Than Encrypted Telegrams 133

Mr. Wang continued, "The messages transmitted by ordinary radios can be received by anyone with a radio. The secret wireless telephone that I invented has special devices for both transmission and reception and cannot be received by ordinary radios. Its structure is very simple, making it suitable for all military command and order purposes. The military telegrams currently sent, even with encryption, are often easily deciphered, and the risk is even greater if the codebook is lost. I cannot disclose the detailed principles, structure, and usage because they are military secrets."

San You Society's Appeal Rejected 143

Dismissal of Workers Without Approval from the Social Affairs Bureau

Workers Residing in the Factory Cannot Be Considered Occupying

Central News Agency, Nanjing, 13th: The Supreme Court has rejected the appeal of the Shanghai San You Society in a case seeking confirmation of the termination of the employment contract, the return of the factory building and equipment. The appellant shall bear the cost of the third instance litigation. The reason is that the company dismissed the workers without the approval of the Social Affairs Bureau, so the employment contract has not been legally terminated. Moreover, according to Article 27 of the Factory Law, the factory must give prior notice to the workers if it wants to terminate the contract. Even if it publishes an advertisement, it cannot be considered a statement of termination of the employment contract. Before the employment contract is terminated, the factory workers' residence in the factory cannot be considered an occupation of the factory property and equipment. The original judgment is correct in all respects.

The funds are set at 100,000 yuan and will be allocated from a charitable fund.

Investigation of Factory Boiler Explosions 145

According to the records of the Municipal Council, there have been 11 factory boiler explosions in the past six years, killing 89 people and injuring 72. The most serious incident was the Zhengtaili Factory incident. In total, there were two rubber refining furnace explosions, five boiler explosions, one acetylene gas tank explosion, one glycerine evaporator explosion, one power transformer explosion, and one metal melting vessel explosion. In March 1931, a boiler at a cigarette factory on Jingzhou Road exploded, and the outer shell, which was 6 1/2 feet long and 40 inches in diameter, weighing about one ton, flew 200 yards. According to the post-accident investigation, the safety valve on the boiler was not damaged. The explosion was probably due to a lack of water in the boiler, which was caused by poorly trained managers. In 1930, a worker at a sock factory on Binlang Road was scalded to death by boiling water from the furnace while adding coal to the furnace. According to the investigation report, it was because the furnace door was not secure, causing water vapor to escape. According to the practice of Western countries, all boilers must be registered and numbered, and inspected annually by experienced engineers, who issue certificates specifying the pressure that the furnace can withstand. Afterwards, inspectors should check the certificate and the pressure gauge on the furnace when they come to the factory. Also, at regular intervals, the boiler must be completely removed for thorough inspection. In Shanghai factories, acetylene and oxygen blowpipes are often used for forging. Acetylene can explode even when it does not come into contact with air, so special attention should be paid to its transport equipment. In rubber refining furnaces, steam and air under pressure are injected, so special attention should be paid to safety measures such as safety valves.

Hat Thief 151

—Sentenced to Imprisonment for One Year and Five Months—

Zhang Desheng, a native of Ningbo, 19 years old, previously served in the military in Nanjing. After retiring, he came to Shanghai last autumn and stayed at a friend's place at No. 91 Xizang Road. Unable to find a job, he often went to the Rongguang Cinema at No. 19 Haining Road to watch movies for entertainment. Later, his purse was empty. Seeing that the felt hats worn by the audience were valuable, he took the opportunity to steal them. From December 22 of last year to the 4th of this year, he stole a total of eight hats, which he pawned in the Wusong Road area, obtaining tens of yuan to spend daily. The day before yesterday afternoon, he went to the cinema again to engage in this activity and was discovered by Zhao Amao and Gu Genxin. They saw him entering in a hurry and leaving with a felt hat in his hand after a while. They immediately questioned him, but he spoke evasively. It was then discovered that the hat belonged to a spectator surnamed Tan. They then handed him over to Chinese detective Wang Guangqi, who took him to the Hongkou Police Station and recovered the original eight stolen felt hats from various pawnshops. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special District Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the cause of the case, saying that the felt hats of the cinema's audience were often disappearing without a trace, so the matter was reported to the management, who instructed the inspectors to pay attention, and the defendant was apprehended. However, the owners of the lost hats could not be found and summoned. Although the cinema had posted advertisements on the glass before the shows to claim the hats, only one owner had come forward. The defendant admitted to the crime in the police station without hesitation. He was asked to be severely punished. The stolen hats were presented for inspection. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he was unemployed and had no other options, so he resorted to this tactic, asking for leniency. Judge Wu Zehan sentenced Zhang Desheng to one year and five months of imprisonment as a warning for habitual theft. The stolen goods will be temporarily stored at the police station for collection.

Plotting to Steal Lumber, First Killing the Watchman 152

Bandits' Vicious Plot Takes a Life

Heavy Sentences for Each After Trial

Bandits Yue Jicai, Liu Yu'an (nicknamed "Tianjin Old Liu"), Lu Fugen (known as "Little Barbarian"), etc., had previously repeatedly sneaked into the Wang Shunxing Lumber Yard on Hed Road to steal lumber, but were always discovered by the yard's watchman, Wang Amei, resulting in failure. They hated him to the bone. Agreeing that they should eliminate Wang if they wanted to steal items from the yard, the group set out from a certain place after 9 PM on January 7 of this year, each carrying an ax and a bag of lime. They went straight to Wang Maoshun's lumber yard. When they arrived, they swarmed forward, first throwing the bag of lime to blind Wang Amei, then using axes to chop him wildly, killing him instantly, before fleeing in a burst of noise. Later, the Xinzha Police Station successively arrested the murderers and recovered two axes and a bag of lime. After the investigation confirmed the facts, the Public Works Department lawyer Wang Yaotang filed a lawsuit based on the charge of premeditated murder. Judge Qian Wenji of the First Special District Court completed the investigation. Yesterday morning, the court session was held and it was announced that Liu Yu'an was sentenced to life imprisonment for the crime of premeditated murder, Yue Jicai was sentenced to twenty years of imprisonment for the crime of premeditated murder, and Lu Fugen was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for the crime of joint murder. The axes and other murder weapons were confiscated.

Teahouse Waiter Dies Suddenly After Collapsing 153

Zhang Lansheng, a native of Yuyao, Zhejiang, 24 years old, had been working as a waiter in the rooftop garden of the New World Company on Nanjing Road. Yesterday afternoon, around 2 PM, Zhang was serving in the garden.
