Talking Points

Many Emperors in Jinan 236

— Xiao Zhi

A recent news report about the busting of someone claiming to be emperor in Jinan was quite hilarious. The gist is: Wang, an unemployed vagrant, deemed himself quite remarkable and had "emperor" thoughts. In February, he discovered a supposed "dragon robe" in his courtyard and thought it was heaven's will, thus following heaven's mandate and enthroning himself, using insane ramblings to mislead the public, gathering hundreds of believers, and dispatching two so-called "military advisors" to acquire all sorts of instruments in preparation for an auspicious enthronement day. County Magistrate Fan and a certain regiment commander stationed in the area were alerted to this, so this "quasi-emperor" who hadn't even sat on the dragon throne got to experience the taste of iron bars.

This matter is slightly similar to the demon bandit case in Jinan this past December of someone self-proclaimed "Three Emperors." But the ringleader of the "Three Emperors" case, the fake "Heavenly Emperor" Li Lecuan, was able to have the "Imperial Concubine" flatter, so now he has his freedom. Wang is now in the military tribunal awaiting trial, it's unknown how he will be sentenced, but I suspect Wang could copy the "Imperial Concubine" Li's tactic of sweetly saying "Lord Fan will approve my application" "I will secure your throne" "Please release my Great Royal Eight" and that will elicit "boisterous laughter," confiscate the "dragon robe and instruments" and show "deep sympathy for his nerves being stimulated", and return our "quasi-emperor" Wang with freedom.

Though these comical events stem from ignorance, they are indeed "worthy of deep sympathy," but there are many subtle clues that make one suspect that the enemy is planning trouble behind the scenes! Look, Li Lecuan's confession stated that "Xuantong sent someone to connect and promised Japan would provide guns and cannons," and where did this "dragon robe" come from? Was it really a "heavenly" gift? Even if it was a "neighbor's prank," where did the neighbor get this "dragon robe"? In my imagination, this "dragon robe" must be studded with pearls and treasures, at least it should be a "red satin" with "gold thread Xiang embroidery" like the grand robes worn by fake emperors on the stage. Who would be willing to spend so much on a "prank"? If it was a "neighbor's prank," where did these hundreds of believers come from? ... Investigating layer by layer, do we treat this as a simple case of "severely stimulated nerves" and give it "special sympathy"? Or do we faintly see a huge hand pulling the strings behind this puppet?

Arts

Bamboo Branch Ballads 237

— Niu

Young Marshal Zhang boarded a ship to Italy the other night, and he took his summer palace paintings and calligraphies. Government officials accompanied him to the pier to send him off. I was moved to pen a few lines in his honor:

The young marshal has a good time.

With butterflies and mandarin ducks by his side.

He packs up the forbidden city treasures,

Set sail to Europe at his side.

There were no bells of war,

So he abandoned the country for peace.

He takes with him ashes,

To bury the ones he may find abroad.

The flowers are the same as home,

But the clouds and rain over here are a bit strange.

Who can tell me if being an outsider feels like here,

If there are any girls for him at the clubs.

He has led the world astray in his time,

But even now the old men are afraid of his wrath.

Shouldering the weight of the past,

In Italy he'll have more than enough.

His complexion looks pale,

His body covered in scars.

If you ask him what happened to him,

He'll say it was a rainy day.

Another Shortcut to Converting Tael to Yuan 238

— Wei

I was inspired by Mr. Ouyang's "715 Shortcut for Converting Tael to Yuan" chart in the April 6th issue. The calculation method is ingenious and admirable! However, it is my humble opinion that this type of formula, similar to the return of a pearl, is difficult to remember without thorough study. Moreover, the calculation involves too many digits, making it inconvenient to apply, and still feels somewhat lacking. Based on my research, I have derived another shortcut, briefly described below for readers' study.

Shortcut: Multiply the number of taels you want to convert to silver dollars by 1.4 to get a product (the number of silver dollars). Then, subtract one-thousandth of this product (that is, the number obtained by moving the decimal point of the product three places to the left) from this product to get the desired number of silver dollars. For example, to convert 367 taels of standard silver to silver dollars using the legal rate of 715, the formula is as follows:

367 × 1.4 = 513.88 yuan

513.80 yuan - 0.5138 yuan = 513.2862 yuan

According to comparisons, the result obtained using this shortcut differs from the result obtained by dividing the number of taels by the legal rate by no more than a few cents when converting to hundreds of silver dollars, and no more than a few tenths of a cent when converting to tens of thousands of silver dollars. I have tested it many times and found it to be consistently accurate. However, it should be noted that when applying this method, the legal rate of 715 must be used, otherwise the multiplier should change accordingly. I will not elaborate on the mathematical principles involved in this method due to limited space in this publication.

Shanghai Morning Talks 239

— Ping

Returning from the Typesetting Room

Some have written much about Shanghai Night Talks, saying the nights in Shanghai are a paradise above hell. I think Shanghai Morning Talks are equally worth writing about because the mornings in Shanghai are a hell within paradise. When the pleasure-seekers end their nightlife, the working class—at least the producers—begin their efforts. Let's start with our work because there are quite a few people in Shanghai who depend on it for a living.

The manager posted a notice in the editor's office glass cabinet stating that the newspaper would change its typesetting style starting tomorrow. As a result, all the talents in our editorial office personally went to the typesetting room. Usually, local news, financial columns, and supplements are sent to the typesetting workers for typesetting in advance. Today, after receiving a call from the manager, none of the proofs were put on the racks after proofreading. When we finished editing the telegrams and arrived at the typesetting room, it was already past one o'clock. Everyone yawned while typesetting, not caring whether it looked better than the previous style. When the work was completed, it was almost dawn the next day.

"Damn it, isn't the circulation good? Why change the damn style!" Little Chen adjusted his wide-framed glasses on his nose, muttering to himself as he stepped out of the typesetting room. Old He, nicknamed "Pretty Boy," had snowflakes and sweat frozen together on his face, constantly wiping it with a handkerchief.

"Little Chen, isn't that appointment at the Carlton again early tomorrow (today)? Getting a raise is always like pulling silk from a cocoon. A good newspaper still has to come up with this and that. He sleeps with his mistress while making others stay up all night!" Old He continued to grumble.

Looking around, there wasn't a single rickshaw in sight, unsure if it was the shift change. We had no choice but to move forward with heavy steps.

"Old He, any romantic encounters?"

Old He didn't answer. The sky was just beginning to lighten, and the streetlights had lost their glow. Three long shadows lay across the road, moving gently forward, like a ghostly, gloomy hell.

After dragging ourselves across two streets, we discovered a new continent—several rickshaws were coming towards us with their poles. The three of us jumped into the rickshaws in unison, touched our hat brims, and nodded. The rickshaw pullers took off running.

Sitting in the rickshaw, my eyelids felt even heavier, so I closed my eyes drowsily. Feeling the rickshaw rolling on the asphalt road was exceptionally comfortable.

As if in a dream, I suddenly heard urgent footsteps chasing from behind. I thought, "Winter has passed smoothly, wouldn't it be a laughingstock to run into a pig-slaughtering scene in spring?" My heart pounded, completely dispelling my sleepiness. I listened intently as the sound approached from behind. I pressed hard on the footboard, and the rickshaw puller, taken aback by the sudden force, turned his head and asked, "Isn't it the Route de Saipo?" He thought he had taken the wrong route. I couldn't tell him the reason for pressing the footboard and angrily said, "Pull faster!" But in the midst of the question and answer, the rickshaw behind had already caught up to mine. The rickshaw puller's torn shoes hit the asphalt road, making a sound like horses' hooves. I turned my head, secretly laughing at my misunderstanding. The passenger in the other rickshaw was smiling at me—a protagonist from Shanghai Night Talks, a Dancing Girl. My rickshaw puller, after being overtaken, muttered, "Little Sanzi, come on!" They pulled the rickshaws like a race, and the dancing girl laughed, shaking in the rickshaw.

"Where's the dance hall?" I asked.

"Great Eastern."

Her rickshaw slowly moved ahead, and the rickshaw puller triumphantly shouted, "Little Liuzi, come on!"

She turned her head, raised her Xiangling leather suitcase, and waved to me, signaling goodbye.

I saw her permed hair disappear as the sun was about to rise.

Studying While Defecating 240

— Ziyang

Nowadays, people often say that Chinese students are too lazy and unwilling to study hard. During class, they are either dozing off or telling jokes, so even university students have poor language skills. Where can China find talent?

These words are indeed true, but I often see students holding a book in their hands while defecating, reading without looking away. This diligent appearance is truly admirable. Therefore, I urge the school authorities to quickly reward defecation. The more one defecates, the more credits one receives. If someone defecates all day long, then he must be "reluctant to put down the book." If Mr. Teng Hong saw this, he would probably praise, "Hui is indeed studious." In this way, the school will be full of diligent students, and there will be no worry about a lack of talent in China. However, it's important not to tear up the toilet paper (In support of the righteous army).

Clerk's Correspondence

A Friend of My Wife 241

Editor:

I currently have a very difficult problem to solve. If you could give me a satisfactory answer in your Clerk's Correspondence column, I would be truly grateful. The facts are as follows: I am twenty-eight years old and work as a clerk in a foreign company. Last autumn, I married a Miss Huang. Before we got married, I met her closest sister, Miss Yang, through her introduction. Later, we met several times at Miss Huang's house, but we only nodded in greeting. Since we got married, Miss Yang has often visited my wife, so I have become more familiar with her than before. As time flowed by, she has now shown me a very affectionate attitude and often asks me to go out to the park or see movies with her. Because I couldn't refuse out of politeness, I went to see a movie with her once. But my wife doesn't know about this. If my wife found out, wouldn't she become jealous? But if I break off with Miss Yang, I would feel sorry for her. I am now in a dilemma. I earnestly

ask you for a satisfactory solution. Wishing you

Spiritual Happiness Chen Yingqiu

Editor's Note: Mr. Chen is a married man. If he pursues love with his wife's friend, Miss Yang, even though she certainly already knows that you are a married man and you have not deceived her, it may not be entirely unjustifiable legally or morally. However, since she is very affectionate towards you, you should consider her feelings and prevent her from regretting it later. Therefore, you should find a way to avoid this entanglement

Completely wash away humiliation, and fill the heroic Manchurian state.

, that is really the right thing to do. However, if you reject her directly and frankly, it may leave too deep a wound in her heart, and it may not be very appropriate. Based on our inference, Mr. Chen must be an understanding and interesting man—hiding it from his wife and going to see a movie with her—so he was able to win Miss Yang's deep affection. Understanding this, Mr. Chen's problem will be solved easily. You might as well pretend to be an insensitive fool. When she asks you out, ask her to invite your wife to go with you. This way, on the one hand, you can show that you and your wife have a deep affection, making her feel that there is no opportunity. On the other hand, with such a bodyguard wife, there is nothing to fear. Seeing your actions, she will naturally gradually cool down her feelings. Finally, we believe that if there are other promising young men among Mr. Chen's friends who are still seeking a partner, Mr. Chen might as well introduce them. In short, she wants secrecy, but you must be open. This is the clever way to deal with this problem that we have come up with.

Self-Employment Introductions

—This newspaper reserves the right to choose or reject submissions to this column—

Mr. Jin, from Hangzhou, nineteen years old, with a secondary school education, enjoys painting, is familiar with the world's book classification methods, and is proficient in Chinese typing. He has worked as a trainee in the editorial department of a bookstore for three years and is willing to take on the above position. Fiction

Time in a Dream (Continued 28) 242

— Qin Shouou

Ms. Liu didn't forbid him, but she set three rules. First, no drinking during the day; second, no going to bars; and third, only high-quality brandy was allowed. Wu Yi fully accepted the second and third rules because the location and choice of alcohol wouldn't affect the principle of drinking, so there was no need to haggle over it. However, the first rule—no drinking during the day—was truly impossible to obey. Yet, he couldn't openly object, so he had to imitate the provincial chairmen's attitude towards central government decrees, outwardly compliant but inwardly defiant. Knowing that Ms. Liu wouldn't come to the school, he bought as much brandy as possible and hid it in the lounge, drinking freely at any time. Fortunately, he drank from a glass, so his colleagues thought he was drinking tea, and no one paid attention. They let him get drunk, lie down at his desk for a nap, and drift off into a dream, unaware that the east had already darkened.

Drinking, sleeping... good times passed by in a dream-like life, gradually transforming a lively and excited Dr. Wu into a silent and tranquil middle-aged man. His former colleagues were all taking advantage of their positions as professors at political schools to advance their careers and make a fortune, each displaying their abilities. Only Wu Yi still held his brandy bottle, guarding his old position for more than ten years. But even a dull person has dull luck. Because he was able to be so content and patient, he was noticed by a newly appointed Minister of Education, who thought that he wanted to find a puppet who was both experienced and could be controlled, and only Dr. Wu was the right person. So he exceptionally appreciated him and appointed him as the president of National University XX.

After the appointment letter arrived, Wu Yi had to reluctantly abandon the desk at which he had been drinking and napping almost every day for more than ten years and step into the president's office of University XX to begin his new life of changing the soup but not the medicine.

Although most university presidents do not teach classes, in principle, they should be responsible for everything and would not be so idle. However, Wu Yi was a puppet that Minister XX had deliberately created. The hiring of professors was handled by Minister XX's cousin—the head of the professorate—and the economic management was the sole responsibility of Minister XX's brother-in-law—the director of administrative affairs. Wu Yi was just a symbolic leader, so other than signing and sealing documents, he had virtually nothing to do.

Movie Special

The First Movies Imported into China 243

— Fei Wo

Thirty coppers to watch a show on Fourth Horse Road

In recent years, the film industry in China has been developing rapidly day by day. The public's interest in movies is also growing stronger every day. Tracing back through history, foreign movies were imported into China roughly in three stages: the first stage was Hong Kong, the second stage was Shanghai, and the third stage was the cities of Beijing, Tianjin, Hankou…and inland areas. The first import to Shanghai was about thirty years ago. A foreigner with light blue glasses suddenly came to Shanghai, carrying a half-old movie machine. He also hired several red-headed Indians to beat drums and play western horns, making a great commotion every day at the Shenping Teahouse on Fourth Horse Road. At that time, Shanghai was not yet very prosperous, and only a small number of Westerners were doing business in Shanghai. Shanghai people were very curious when they suddenly saw this foreigner. But the old gentleman set up a white bamboo cloth on his table, twisted the machine (still using dry batteries), and as if by magic, mountains and rivers, figures, and dark shadows all appeared one after another on the white cloth. The people who gathered to watch were all dumbfounded, thinking it was the newly arrived "Western mirror," but they couldn't guess what was being sold in the gourd. This was the initial spark for the import of movies into China.

Slowly, people learned the name of the foreigner. He was from Spain and was called Soma. He was also the first person to establish a movie theater in Shanghai. He first came to Shanghai around 1903. At that time, it cost thirty coppers to watch his "Western mirror" movie, and you could only watch it once. If you wanted to watch it again, you had to pay again. People who paid thirty coppers to watch his movies still talk about it with great enthusiasm. Later, because his business was thriving, he opened a movie theater on Zhabei Road, which is now the Hongkou Grand Theater. This was the first movie theater to appear in Shanghai.

In recent years, the film industry in Shanghai has developed as fast as electricity. Advertisements for movie theater openings can be seen almost everywhere on the streets. Talking about prices, it originally cost thirty coppers, but now it costs at least twenty cents to see a movie, and up to three or four yuan. Compared to then, it's a world apart! I wonder what these moviegoers think about it?

Film Reviews

Review of "A Woman's Shout" 244

— Ling He

Indeed, at a time when dark forces permeate all of China, the cries for "women's liberation" should rise to the sky and stir up a great wave of anger. Their suffering, their struggles, undoubtedly, they must use their own strength to open up a bright path.

Then, "A Woman's Shout" is a work that has been stirred up in this upsurge. If it can truly represent this liberation movement, even taking on the task of guidance, then it is definitely what Chinese audiences desperately need.

But what does the screenwriter and director Shen Xiling tell us in this film? Ye Lian, from the owning class, suffered from the sacrifices of the "civil war," returned to the countryside, and was robbed by bandits. She had no choice but to escape to the city with her weak sister. In the city, in the factory, she suffered "double oppression" and cried in pain, and also engaged in a powerless struggle. As a result, she woke up from the delusion of love and realized that "personal struggle" was not enough. Then, the subtitles tell us that she should be awakened.

True, in theory, all this is quite correct, and it can also be regarded as an analysis of the complex relations and forms of real society. But according to the evolution of the plot, the protagonist Ye Lian should be a fairly conscious young woman with a strong will in the first part. Later, she should be a resolute resister, and should seek proper steps for liberation. At the same time, since she has been enlightened by the prescient Shao Ying, with her understanding, she would never be so naive as to repeatedly accept the deception and deception of the potluck boss. Here, the script itself is inevitably lacking. As mentioned above, Ye Lian, in Mr. Shen's ideal, has conversely become a very timid woman. She only cries, only grieves, and in the end, she has not "shouted" anything at all. It is only a tragedy that exposes evil forces. Although the play expresses dissatisfaction with evil forces, it is ultimately a powerless elegy.

As for the performance techniques, it is generally passable. Although the handling and editing of the shots are not good, things like birdcages, candles, and cigars are clever. Of course, the whole thing is not particularly brilliant, but because it is her debut work, we don't need to expect too much.

The protagonist, Wang Ying, because of the director's improper command, and because it was also her first time on camera, of course, the performance will not make us very satisfied.

Other aspects, such as scenery and lighting, are not bad. There are a few actors who are too much, too civilized drama-like. In short, we are not completely satisfied with this play, but we have high hopes for the authors of this film. Work hard! Move forward with big strides!

Review of "Red Bottle" Beauty and the Boss 245

— Yi Wen

The play itself: with such a golden world, a society, it will naturally produce such a work. Is a woman just a "red flower vase?"

A noble baron will naturally be pursued by many women. At the same time, he does have the qualifications to play with women. I hope that women who have watched this film will be aware of it.

The whole play can be said to be entirely dialogue. If you close your eyes, you can listen to it as a Radio Drama. Perhaps it is the use of theatrical elements that is too excessive? The special techniques of film have become auxiliary.

Actors: Marlene Dietrich does have a suitable performance, especially the steps from country girl to simple socialite to modern socialite, from ugly to beautiful, which is very appealing to the audience. This can also be said to be the power of the director.

Warren William is also a worthy wealthy entrepreneur. Director: In addition to the above-mentioned closeness to stage plays, this can only be said to be bad in the script the division of scenes and shots is very economical and smooth. However, one of the baron's mistresses is always in the bathtub every time she calls the baron. It is too much. There are many ways to describe this type of woman. Why not change a few ways? Light and photography techniques: This is worth praising, especially the re-shoot in the first few episodes.

After watching: I feel that it is just a scene of play in a golden world. I hope that Chinese women can reflect more deeply after watching it. Are you willing to be a "red flower vase?" Then you will lose your soul.

After Watching "The Brave Man" 246

— Ai Yun

Yue Ming Company used to make a fuss about heroes or burning, but this time it has clearly changed its style.

Its story is entirely in the style of old novels, telling the love story of a young couple, but a warlord's son takes a fancy to the girl and plots to frame the man, threatening the girl to marry him. After the girl agrees to marry him, the young warlord spares the young man's death sentence and changes it to imprisonment. Unexpectedly, on the day of the wedding, the young man escapes from prison, comes and beats the warlord to a pulp, and takes the girl away. The warlord's side is about to send people to hunt them down, but suddenly, the revolution succeeds, the warlord loses power, and the lovers become married. This kind of story can be said to only suit people with ordinary low tastes.

Director Ren Pengnian is a very promising person, but unfortunately, he is limited by the environment, so he has achieved nothing. He also serves as a screenwriter, but it can only be said that he barely fulfills his responsibilities. The interweaving is not good. Many forced slapstick jokes can also elicit laughter from country women or children. The two "fight scenes" are even more vulgar.

The protagonist Wu Lizhu is extremely famous in martial arts films. But it is really difficult for her to act in this play. The male lead Luo Keming is the only young man used by many small companies. His performance is still watchable, but at most, he is the tallest among the dwarfs. I won't talk about the rest.

The photography is very immature. How can I describe the light? It is completely sunlight, but there is very little light from the reflectors. The exterior scenes are okay. But the shots are too poor. The interior scenes are simple, and it can be seen at a glance that they are fake scenes. There are too many subtitles, and they are either too literary or too vulgar.

In terms of the story, performance, and narration, there are many irrational and disconnected places. But I will not discuss them one by one.

As for the film itself, I say it is below the horizontal line. But its trend is not bad, which is not commonly seen in small companies. So I hope the small companies will work hard!

Review of Lotus's Eloquent Tongue 247

— Yan Nan

Introduction This is a film produced by RKO Pictures, originally named Ladies of the Jury, which was released yesterday at the Nanjing Grand Theater. It is only 7,000 feet long, and the details are as follows:

Story A woman is suspected of murdering her husband. Fortunately, a female juror is a friend of this woman and knows that she has been wronged. So, she uses her lotus-like eloquent tongue to persuade the other jurors with her words. She also hires a detective under a false name. In order to understand the truth, those jurors go to the home of the murdered person to find out what happened. Inadvertently, they discover a man hidden there—the maid's lover. They take the maid and the man to court, and the innocent woman is finally acquitted.

Plot It can only be considered an ordinary film. It is a purely American slapstick film, and it is not interesting to the Chinese. However, I personally see that the jurors personally investigate the case, which clearly shows the protection of civil rights in the United States. There is also the more fair succession of "Anglo-American law" and "jury system."

Director This film could have been shot just as well without a director. Only some interweaving shows the director's skills.

Performance Nothing special. Each actor takes it as a prerequisite to make people laugh. Although there are many commendable slapstick actions, there is nothing to talk about in terms of expression. There is no distinction between hosts and guests in it. The whole film is made up of fragmented close-ups, so the 18 or 19 characters have equal opportunities to perform, which can generally be said to be good.

Others The photography is very ordinary, but it has broken close-ups. The editing is very vivid, and it must be said that the screenwriter is doing a good job. The light is very soft. In terms of scenery, there is only one scene of a car running on the road outside, so there is nothing to say. There are only four rooms inside the court, the jury meeting room, the hotel, and the murdered person's room so simple, which is not found in any American feature film. The pronunciation is very clear.

Personal criticism I can only admit that it is a work below the horizontal line. There are countless unreasonable places in it. It describes an American court as being completely without order. Each actor understands that this is a battle, so what artistic meaning can be said?

Copies The first newsreel is not bad. The second slapstick short film, although it is chaotic, is very humorous and can make people happy.

Review of "Laughter in Hell" 248

— Ao Xiang

Laughterinhell

Hollywood romantic films almost always follow a formula. Boy meets girl, they instantly fall in love, their hearts become entwined; there are no conditions, no necessary cause and effect. After falling in love, there will inevitably be a break-up (either the man or the woman), and after the break-up, they will definitely find another lover and immediately succeed in love again. Then, a Kiss End, and all ends happily. These formulas only differ in minor details. "Laughter in Hell" is also a romantic film produced under this formula.

The story goes like this: Brennan is a young miner, and his mother, while alive, hoped he would become an engineer. Through his father's benevolent cultivation, he soon "achieved his wish." At this point, Brennan's romantic life begins. He falls in love with a girl named Belle, and they get married. However, after the marriage, Belle suddenly changes her heart and has an affair with Brennan's friend Grove. Brennan discovers this secret, and in a fit of anger, he kills them, and is imprisoned. The prison guard happens to be Grove's brother, so Brennan suffers greatly. Eventually, he escapes and seeks refuge in the home of a farm girl, and he immediately falls in love with that farm girl. They drive off in a horse-drawn carriage, supposedly to "create a new life together."

Such a story clearly tells the audience something. We really dare not believe that the so-called love in this film is real, especially the love after Brennan escapes from prison, which seems to have fallen from the sky. Why would that farm girl suddenly love a down-and-out prisoner? If it's said to be sympathy, isn't that farm girl even more humanitarian than the Virgin Mary?

The director's technique is quite successful. The entire film's atmosphere is made very tense, and the choice of background and the mood of the plot are also very harmonious. The actor who plays Brennan, Pat O'Brien, is naturally the most successful. The others are also quite competent. The constant kissing in the film can be said to be a "feature." The depiction of the abuse of prisoners in the jail is vivid. Here, we see a dark side of the so-called "American Land of the Free!"

The Film Novel Y慾 Tarakanova (2) 249

— Mei Hua

Gypsy girls, originally drifting from east to west without a fixed place, naturally do not know their own origins. Xiao Falov said to her very modestly, "I am a count, and I know very well that you are the daughter of Queen Elizabeth. You were driven out by Catherine since you were young. Now, the people of Russia, who doesn't hope you will return? I am someone who has received great favor from Queen Elizabeth, I must help you succeed!"

This Gypsy girl, her blood filled with jumping and joy, she fantasized about the happiness of the future, fantasized about herself becoming Catherine's replacement. Therefore, she agreed, she agreed to everything Xiao Falov arranged.

On the light blue Italian coast, Xiao Falov arranged a magnificent palace for this Gypsy girl, no, she is now Princess Tarakanova (this is Princess Bossetti's real name, people in the world know Tarakanova, but do not know Bossetti). Surrounded by countless warriors and countless palace maids, Princess Tarakanova carried out her enthronement ceremony. The residents of Ragusa were deeply interested in this beautiful foreign princess, and they also held grand carnivals like crazy, holding extremely lively picnics, making a princess transformed from a vagrant girl as happy as if she were falling into a beautiful dream! Especially proud was Xiao Falov, his plan to overthrow Catherine had already achieved half, and when all aspects of the connection were mature, he could launch a large-scale attack on Catherine. This news spread to Russia, spread to Catherine's ears, causing an unusual rage. She decided to trick Princess Tarakanova over before she succeeded. Generals Gray and Orlov accepted Catherine's secret order, boarded a white warship, and went to lure Princess Tarakanova.

On the light blue sea, a beautiful palace floated up, Princess Tarakanova was having a pink dream; the people were celebrating and rejoicing as if drunk: "Beautiful, beautiful princess, you are the one we admire." (To be continued)
